    21	export const RULE_KINDS = ['palette', 'type', 'spacing', 'component'] as const;
    22	
    23	export type DesignRuleKind = (typeof RULE_KINDS)[number];
    24	
    25	/**
    26	 * A rule's link to live CSS: a path to an author-written CSS file (relative to
    27	 * the spec file) plus the selector the rule is anchored to. The selector may be
    28	 * multi-token (descendant combinators); the path is the first whitespace-free

    31	export interface CssLink {

    34	}

     1	/**
     2	 * File-level entry to the design-language spec check — the enforcement seam
     3	 * the `/design-control:translate-design-language` skill (and the
     4	 * `bin/check-design-spec` shim) route EVERY spec draft through, hand-authored
     5	 * or engine-accelerated alike. Mirrors `@/authoring/lint-file` for wireframes:
     6	 * a thin composition of the existing axes, no parallel validation path.
     7	 */
     8	
     9	import { readFileSync } from 'node:fs';
    10	import { dirname, resolve } from 'node:path';
    11	import {
    12	  checkCssLinkLiveness,
    13	  checkLinkLiveness,
    14	  type SkippedLink,
    15	} from '@/design-language/link-liveness';
    16	import { parseDesignSpec } from '@/design-language/schema';
    17	import type { DesignSpecFinding, ParsedDesignSpec } from '@/design-language/types';
    18	
    19	export interface DesignSpecCheckResult {
    20	  /** True iff findings is empty (skipped links stay green but visible). */
    21	  readonly ok: boolean;
    22	  readonly spec: ParsedDesignSpec;
    23	  /** Schema findings followed by link-liveness findings. */
    24	  readonly findings: readonly DesignSpecFinding[];
    25	  readonly skipped: readonly SkippedLink[];
    26	}
    27	
    28	/**
    29	 * Check a design-language spec FILE: read it, validate the markdown schema,
    30	 * then check link-liveness with css paths resolved against the spec file's
    31	 * own directory. Liveness runs over the valid rules AND the parse result's
    32	 * auxiliary css links (links housed in structurally-invalid / duplicate
    33	 * sections), so a schema defect and a dead link on the same section surface
    34	 * in ONE run — never in fix-and-rerun waves. Fails loud on an unreadable
    35	 * file — a missing spec is an error, never a clean verdict.
    36	 */
    37	export function checkDesignSpecFile(filePath: string): DesignSpecCheckResult {
    38	  const absolute = resolve(filePath);
    39	  const markdown = readFileSync(absolute, 'utf8');
    40	  const parsed = parseDesignSpec(markdown);
    41	  const baseDir = dirname(absolute);
    42	  const liveness = checkLinkLiveness(parsed.spec, baseDir);
    43	  const auxiliary = checkCssLinkLiveness(parsed.auxiliaryCssLinks, baseDir);
    44	  const findings = [...parsed.findings, ...liveness.findings, ...auxiliary.findings];
    45	  return {
    46	    ok: findings.length === 0,
    47	    spec: parsed.spec,
    48	    findings,
    49	    skipped: [...liveness.skipped, ...auxiliary.skipped],
    50	  };
    51	}
    52	
    53	/** Line-oriented output sink, injected so the CLI core is testable. */
    54	export interface CliIo {
    55	  out(line: string): void;
    56	  err(line: string): void;
    57	}
    58	
    59	const USAGE = 'usage: check-design-spec <design-language-spec.md>';
    60	
    61	/**
    62	 * CLI core behind `bin/check-design-spec`. Exit-code contract (the skill's
    63	 * gate, same shape as check-wireframe):
    64	 *   0 — spec green (zero findings; skipped links are reported but green)
    65	 *   1 — findings present, or the file could not be read (descriptive error;
    66	 *       never a fabricated verdict)
    67	 *   2 — usage error
    68	 */
    69	export function runCheckDesignSpec(argv: readonly string[], io: CliIo): number {
    70	  if (argv.length !== 1) {
    71	    io.err(USAGE);
    72	    return 2;
    73	  }
    74	  const filePath = argv[0];
    75	  let result: DesignSpecCheckResult;
    76	  try {
    77	    result = checkDesignSpecFile(filePath);
    78	  } catch (error) {
    79	    io.err(error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error));
    80	    return 1;
    81	  }
    82	  for (const skip of result.skipped) {
    83	    io.out(
    84	      `note: rule "${skip.ruleId}" link "${skip.link.path} ${skip.link.selector}" is a non-CSS target — reported unchecked, does not establish link-liveness (this check validates selectors in author-written .css sources only; CSS-in-JS / utility-framework / CSS-Modules targets are outside its validated scope).`,
    85	    );
    86	  }
    87	  if (result.ok) {
    88	    io.out(`${filePath}: spec green — 0 findings (${result.spec.rules.length} rule(s))`);
    89	    return 0;
    90	  }
    91	  for (const finding of result.findings) {
    92	    io.err(`${finding.rule}${finding.ruleId ? ` (rule: ${finding.ruleId})` : ''}: ${finding.message}`);
    93	  }
    94	  io.err(`${filePath}: ${result.findings.length} finding(s)`);
    95	  return 1;
    96	}

     1	---
     2	name: translate-design-language
     3	description: Draft or maintain the project's design-language spec — the hand-authorable markdown artifact that anchors visual identity (palette/type/spacing tokens + signature components, each rule linked to live CSS + ≥1 example). Hand-authoring is the default and needs NO engine; the optional /frontend-design accelerator drafts from approved wireframe intent and is judged by the same check-design-spec gate.
     4	---
     5	
     6	# /design-control:translate-design-language
     7	
     8	Author or update the **design-language spec** for this project. The spec is the
     9	visual-*letter* artifact of the design-control discipline: the durable home for
    10	visual identity (the lo-fi wireframe carries UX *spirit* and is structurally
    11	incapable of carrying visual detail). Every rule binds to reality — a live CSS
    12	file + selector, ≥1 current example — so the spec cannot quietly drift into
    13	fiction the way a mockup's incidental polish does.
    14	
    15	> Per the plugin thesis (`DESIGN-DISCIPLINE-THESIS.md`): policy is enforced by
    16	> a process, not a rule. "Each rule links to live CSS" is not a convention the
    17	> author is trusted to follow — it is mechanically enforced by the
    18	> `check-design-spec` gate (schema + static link-liveness), which every draft
    19	> MUST pass before it may be presented.
    20	
    21	## Spec convention (hand-authorable markdown)
    22	
    23	One markdown file (conventionally `design-language.md` in the operator's chosen
    24	design docs directory). Rules are declared under ATX headings, fields are
    25	bullets with a closed key set:
    26	
    27	```markdown
    28	# Design language: <project>
    29	
    30	## Palette
    31	
    32	### rule: ink-primary
    33	- kind: palette
    34	- css: styles/studio.css .btn-primary
    35	- example: dashboard compose button uses .btn-primary
    36	- do: Use the ink palette for every primary action.
    37	- don't: Never introduce raw hex blues outside the palette tokens.
    38	```
    39	
    40	- `kind:` — one of `palette` / `type` / `spacing` / `component` (the closed
    41	  vocabulary; `component` is the signature-component class).
    42	- `css: <path> <selector>` — ≥1 per rule; the path is relative to the spec
    43	  file; the selector must be **defined in that author-written CSS source**
    44	  (checked statically — no app boot). Non-CSS targets (CSS-in-JS, utility
    45	  frameworks, CSS-Modules) are reported as unchecked notes and do not
    46	  establish link-liveness.
    47	- `example:` — ≥1 per rule (a rule with zero examples is rejected). Presence
    48	  is structural; whether the example still matches live UI is
    49	  `spec-truthfulness`, a separate concern this gate does not check.
    50	- `do:` / `don't:` — ≥1 guidance line per rule.
    51	
    52	## Procedure
    53	
    54	1. **Locate or create the spec file.** One spec per design language; do not
    55	   fork per-surface copies. If the operator has no spec yet, scaffold the
    56	   heading + one rule per obvious anchor (masthead, primary action, body type)
    57	   directly from the live CSS — with the operator naming the files that count
    58	   as design-language source.
    59	
    60	2. **Author or update rules — manual path (default, requires NO engine).** The
    61	   operator (or the agent under operator direction) writes the rules by hand:
    62	   pick the selector in live CSS the rule is anchored to, cite ≥1 current
    63	   example, state the do/don't. Scaffold completion never depends on engine
    64	   presence — this path never calls the engine preflight.
    65	
    66	3. **Optional engine accelerator.** Only if the operator asks for it: gate on
    67	   `preflightEngine` (`@/engine-adapter`, method `translate-design-language`)
    68	   — absence fails loud naming the remedy — then request a draft from the
    69	   engine (input: the approved wireframe intent + the live CSS files the
    70	   operator names). **Engine output gets zero trust:** it lands in the same
    71	   file and is judged by the same gate as a hand-authored draft. Engine
    72	   conformance (`@/engine-adapter/conformance`) is exercised only when the
    73	   engine is present — never stub it to simulate presence.
    74	
    75	4. **Validation gate — the non-negotiable step.** Run:
    76	
    77	   ```bash
    78	   plugins/design-control/bin/check-design-spec <path/to/design-language.md>
    79	   ```
    80	
    81	   - Exit `0` (spec green, zero findings) → the draft may be presented.
    82	     Read any `does not establish link-liveness` notes aloud to the operator —
    83	     a skipped link is visible scope, not silent coverage.
    84	   - Exit `1` → fix every finding and re-run. A dead selector means either the
    85	     rule rots (fix the link) or the CSS moved (update the rule) — NEVER
    86	     delete the rule just to silence the finding; that decision is the
    87	     operator's.
    88	
    89	5. **Present and stop.** Show the operator the green spec (path + `0 findings`
    90	   output + rule count). The operator owns acceptance; implementation against
    91	   the spec and refereeing are separate steps of the loop, not this skill's
    92	   job.
    93	
    94	## What this skill does NOT do
    95	
    96	- It does not author wireframes (`/design-control:wireframe`), implement, or
    97	  referee.
    98	- It does not boot the app, capture screenshots, or verify that examples still
    99	  match live UI (that is `spec-truthfulness`, which no step of this skill
   100	  performs).
   101	- It does not skip the gate for engine-authored drafts — same gate, same
   102	  checker, zero findings.

codex
I’m also checking whether the spec’s “relative CSS path” contract is actually enforced. The parser preserves the first token without validating relativity, and the liveness layer resolves it directly, so absolute and parent-traversal paths are accepted as if they were portable spec links.
codex
### Selector argument normalization makes distinct state selectors interchangeable

Finding-ID: AUDIT-BARRAGE-codex-01
Status:     open
Severity:   medium
Surface:    plugins/design-control/src/design-language/link-liveness.ts:157-180

`cssDefinesSelector` strips string contents and functional pseudo-class arguments from both the query and source prelude before matching. The comment explicitly states the consequence: a query for one quoted attribute value matches a source rule with a different value, and a full functional-pseudo selector can match a source rule with different arguments. That means `.chip[data-state="open"]` can be accepted when the CSS only defines `.chip[data-state="closed"]`, and `.real:not(.ghost)` can be accepted when only `.real:not(.other)` exists.

Blast radius is medium: this creates a false green for common component-state selectors, so the checker can say a design-language rule is linked to live CSS when the exact state anchor is absent. The user-facing skill still says the selector must be defined in the source, so a downstream agent will not know that state values are ignored. A reasonable correction is to keep string and functional arguments comparable in selector preludes while still excluding declaration strings such as `content: ".ghost"`.

### Absolute CSS paths can pass even though the spec contract says paths are relative

Finding-ID: AUDIT-BARRAGE-codex-02
Status:     open
Severity:   medium
Surface:    plugins/design-control/src/design-language/schema.ts:96-110; plugins/design-control/src/design-language/link-liveness.ts:211-217; plugins/design-control/skills/translate-design-language/SKILL.md:42-46

The skill contract says `css:` paths are relative to the spec file, but the parser accepts the first whitespace-free token without validating it, and liveness passes it directly to `resolve(baseDir, link.path)`. In Node, an absolute path ignores `baseDir`, so `css: /Users/.../studio.css .btn` can go green on the author’s machine while producing a nonportable design-language spec.

Blast radius is medium because deskwork artifacts are collection content, not machine-local state. A green spec with absolute local paths will mislead downstream consumers or fail outside the original checkout. The checker should reject absolute paths as malformed, and probably reject or consciously constrain parent traversal if the intended artifact boundary is the spec directory or collection root.

### Temporal scope wording still remains in the audited diff

Finding-ID: AUDIT-BARRAGE-codex-03
Status:     open
Severity:   low
Surface:    plugins/design-control/specs/001-design-control/tasks.md:176-191; plugins/design-control/src/design-language/schema.ts:15-18; plugins/design-control/src/design-language/link-liveness.ts:9-15; plugins/design-control/src/design-language/types.ts:42-45

The operator-facing skill and CLI text were rewritten to capability statements, but the workplan and design-language source comments still retain the temporal scope phrasing called out by the audit prompt’s hard constraint. The visible task record at `tasks.md:176-191` still carries that language several times, and source comments repeat the same framing in the schema, liveness, and shared type docs.

Blast radius is low because the runtime behavior is visible and the CLI now uses stable capability language. The issue is documentation discipline: future agents reading the workplan or comments can reintroduce the same phrasing into operator-facing surfaces. A reasonable correction is to use capability wording consistently, matching the skill and CLI text.
